  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_205cb3a5-9d15-46d3-b3bf-438f98b06c3e'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer6899551739500947440">Young Lerris is dissatisfied with his life and trade, and yearns to find a place in the world better suited to his skills and temperament. But in Recluce a change in circumstances means taking one of two options: permanent exile from Recluce or the dangergeld, a complex, rule-laden wanderjahr in the lands beyond Recluce, with the aim of learning how the world works and wha</span>
  <span id="freeText6899551739500947440" style="display:none">Young Lerris is dissatisfied with his life and trade, and yearns to find a place in the world better suited to his skills and temperament. But in Recluce a change in circumstances means taking one of two options: permanent exile from Recluce or the dangergeld, a complex, rule-laden wanderjahr in the lands beyond Recluce, with the aim of learning how the world works and what his place in it might be. Many do not survive. Lerris chooses dangergeld. When Lerris is sent into intensive training for his quest, it soon becomes clear that he has a natural talent for magic. And he will need magic in the lands beyond, where the power of the Chaos Wizards reigns unchecked. Though it goes against all of his instincts, Lerris must learn to use his powers in an orderly way before his wanderjahr, or fall prey to Chaos.</span>

<div id="review_108099251" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108099251" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108099251?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">heroic fantasy readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books) by: </span>
      Jim
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=warrior-woman">warrior-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=animal-character-steals-the-show">animal-character-steals-the-show</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroic-fantasy">heroic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=older-woman-younger-man">older-woman-younger-man</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108099251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6631705454672195995">This was a book where patience proves to be a virtue. It started very slowly, with an almost tedious amount of detail. As I continued to read, it started to make sense. <br/><br/>This is a book about the battle between two opposing forces: chaos and order. The tedious amount of detail really ties into this story, for it defined the foundation of Recluce. Recluce is a city of almost pure order. Everything is so perfect and ordered that it is perceived as being boring to our hero, Lerris. Any persons who co</span>
  <span id="freeText6631705454672195995" style="display:none">This was a book where patience proves to be a virtue. It started very slowly, with an almost tedious amount of detail. As I continued to read, it started to make sense. <br /><br />This is a book about the battle between two opposing forces: chaos and order. The tedious amount of detail really ties into this story, for it defined the foundation of Recluce. Recluce is a city of almost pure order. Everything is so perfect and ordered that it is perceived as being boring to our hero, Lerris. Any persons who compromise that order are exiled. Our hero is such a person. But, like any good heroic fantasy, this reluctant, unlikely hero does save the day.<br /><br />Lerris was a bit annoying at first, like one of those eternally bored youngsters that made my life miserable when I taught. I don't think I've ever seen the word 'boring' so much in my life. When I was a kid, I was not allowed to be 'bored', so I don't have much patience for people who go through life bored with everything. Fortunately, I came to see how this plays a role in the story. Lerris is looking for answers. He's like the kid who always asks 'why' about everything, wanted to be told instead of finding out the answers for himself. His exile from Recluce turns out to be the making of him. He finds a strength and a purpose over the course of this novel that can only be gained the hard way, through action and practice.<br /><br />At first, I didn't think Mr. Modesitt's style of writing was going to work for me, but then I began to appreciate it. His attention to detail is very important to the narrative. I especially liked his descriptions of woodworking. I am not very good with my hands, despite being a decent artist and gardener. I do respect those who can build functional things with their hands. Lerris's approach to woodworking--initially one of boredom and disinterest, which changed to one of intense focus and commitment to perfection--was a metaphor for his maturation from boy to man. He has a hard, often lonely road ahead of him in this novel. Seeing that slow, often painful growth made me come to love him as a hero. He showed that his heart was in the right place, although he seemed so disinterested and self-absorbed initially.<br /><br />The magic system was very interesting. It turned a a big thing on its head as far as conventions: the black wizards are the good wizards, and the white wizards are the evil wizards. That was an unique twist that I liked. I was surprised that I figured out some of how the chaos versus order dynamic worked. I was putting the pieces together along with Lerris. I liked how the order in persons and things were manipulated by Lerris and his eventual mentor, gray (mostly black but a little white) wizard, Justen. That was their power as order-masters. And it wasn't just a matter of creating things to solve problems. If done wrongly or for the wrong motives, this could become an act of chaos. Lerris had to continually weigh his actions to make sure he wasn't doing that. As I read, I wondered what could and couldn't be done and stay on the side of order. <br /><br />Although this story is focused on Lerris, there are some interesting secondary characters, and quite a lot of strong, well-developed women characters. I liked that the women were in powerful roles, often serving in the military and as soldiers. Krystal turned out to be a good character, showing her own evolution in character for the best. And I loved Lerris trusty mountain pony, Gairloch. He's quite the boon companion.<br /><br />I am the risk of being long-winded, so I'll bring this review to a close. This was a very good book. I'm glad I hung in there and kept reading past the slow beginning, and that I paid attention. Mr. Modesitt lays a powerful foundation for this story, and everything ties in together. I appreciate being recommended this story by a fellow Goodreads friend. I will definitely continue reading this series. Recommended to readers who like an intricate fantasy story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6631705454672195995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer72933510" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17122086932805172677">I debated the rating on this and went with 4.<br/><br/><br/>The above was my original review of this book, I'm a little surprised that it got a vote (LOL). I'm also a little surprised at my comment. In retrospect I like the book much better than my initial impression above. Over the years, the book has apparently gotten better LOL. It stayed with me and I own most of the series...I like it and the series a great deal. I read this book a good many years ago and it launched me off into tracking down the Recluse </span>
  <span id="freeText17122086932805172677" style="display:none">I debated the rating on this and went with 4.<br /><br /><br />The above was my original review of this book, I'm a little surprised that it got a vote (LOL). I'm also a little surprised at my comment. In retrospect I like the book much better than my initial impression above. Over the years, the book has apparently gotten better LOL. It stayed with me and I own most of the series...I like it and the series a great deal. I read this book a good many years ago and it launched me off into tracking down the Recluse books or snatching them up as they came out. Modesitt is one of those interesting people who can turn out a lot of books and still have the quality stay high. <br /><br />These are a fantastic fantasy series and worth the read. It rests heavily on character development (though some disagree about this I think the character/s are well drawn and interesting). This/these books have an interesting and "fairly" original magic system that he builds onto rather well later. <br /><br />Second update:<br /><br />I just reread this novel (again) with a group read here and have decided to up the rating to 5 stars. While others have expressed negative opinions of the book it seems every time I read it I like it better. <br /><br />I will note one thing. This time I "read" the audio version of the book. a couple of the other readers in the group noted that all the sound effects in the book annoyed them,(biff, splush, zingggg, swish, etc.). I suppose that I just read over these the first time I read the book as I sometimes do obscenities, oaths or whatever. This time both the fact that I'm listening to the audio and the fact that they had been brought to my attention caused me to notice them. I have to admit there are a lot of them, however far from annoying me now when I hear the exceptional number of sound effects, I tend to crack up. As the boots pulled out of the mud or the wood broke or whatever I'd laugh out loud just noticing it.<br /><br />So, yeah lots of sound effects but still a deeply characterized story and very well told.</span>

<div id="review_30803131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30803131" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30803131?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=sword-sorcery">sword-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30803131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16337566100552363863">He posits an interesting world where Order (Black) & Chaos (White) are separate forces that can be manipulated by humans. Those who wield each, don't generally play well with those who use the opposing force. There is a balance, so both forces gain more play in the world as the other side becomes stronger. Some people are focuses of one or the other, too. It leads to interesting situations.<br/><br/>The world is complex with very real politics, economics, & issues. That's what I like best about them since</span>
  <span id="freeText16337566100552363863" style="display:none">He posits an interesting world where Order (Black) &amp; Chaos (White) are separate forces that can be manipulated by humans. Those who wield each, don't generally play well with those who use the opposing force. There is a balance, so both forces gain more play in the world as the other side becomes stronger. Some people are focuses of one or the other, too. It leads to interesting situations.<br /><br />The world is complex with very real politics, economics, &amp; issues. That's what I like best about them since parallels can easily be drawn to our reality. It's not boring, but full of twists, betrayals, &amp; problems. What's even more real are the way he treats peasants &amp; crafters. Wood &amp; metal working are very well described. Well enough that I'm glad I don't use hide glue &amp; have modern finishes.<br /><br />Throughout the series, his heroes &amp; heroines have to take care of their horses which occasionally slow the frantic pace since they're not just cars with hooves. They get tired, have to be fed, given breaks, &amp; have their stalls mucked out. None of them seem to care for the smell of horse all that much which is rather odd to me. I like it, a good thing since it's the perfume of preference for my wife.<br /><br />In this book, he tells the story from the Order side. He continues this for the next 6 books in published order, until book 8, "The White Order" finally gives us the Chaos side of the story. This is the first of the series published, but is currently next to the last or so in the chronology. He recommends his books be read in the order he wrote them &amp; I have to agree for the first read, but a second round in chronological order is better, though. I've read some books several times. Very enjoyable, a highly recommended series.<br /><br />Since this book is listed first in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41825-the-saga-of-recluce" rel="nofollow noopener">the GR 'Saga of Recluce' list</a> I'm going to put chronological order list here. I wished GR had a chronological list for this series &amp; Rindis <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/216144-the-saga-of-recluse-chronological" rel="nofollow noopener">made it here.</a> <b>Thanks, Rindis!</b> I didn't know how to create it, just this way &amp; Listopia. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/113663.Saga_of_Recluce_Chronological_Reading_Order" rel="nofollow noopener">I created one there</a>, but it can get messed up.<br /><br />Note, this list is subject to change. Modesitt is constantly adding to the series (Amazingly keeping it fresh, too.) &amp; I'll put in the short stories as best I can, too. If anyone can add to or help make this better, please leave a comment about it &amp; I'll tweak as needed. Update: The author himself gave me the chronology for the short stories &amp; has checked this.<br /><br /><b>Current Recluce Chronology</b> (18Jan2018)<br />Books are whole numbers, short stories are fractional.<br /><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29939388.Recluce_Tales_Stories_from_the_World_of_Recluce" title="Recluce Tales Stories from the World of Recluce by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Recluce Tales: Stories from the World of Recluce</a>
</b> are all the Recluce short stories, although some can be found elsewhere, too. I'll note that if I know it. In the book, they're in chronological order save for one &amp; I've inserted them here in their proper places in the list here. Books are grouped by characters/story arcs. (Many thanks to Modesitt for placating my obsessive need.)<br /><b>0.5 - "The Vice Marshal's Trial"</b> Year -300, takes place roughly 300 years before the beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/727699.Magi_i_of_Cyador__The_Saga_of_Recluce___10_" title="Magi'i of Cyador (The Saga of Recluce, #10) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Magi'i of Cyador</a> &amp; is about one aspect of the founding of Cyador. <br /><b>0.6 - "Madness"</b> Year -200, is set about a hundred years after the above. It takes place on the opposite side of Candor, a bit of the early history of Lydiar.<br /><b>0.7 - "The Forest Girl"</b> slightly after the above, back in Cyador, a glimpse into the life of Alyiakal &amp; the Great Forest.<br /><br /><b>0.8</b>"The Choice" - Year -50, takes place about 50 years before the start of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/727699.Magi_i_of_Cyador__The_Saga_of_Recluce___10_" title="Magi'i of Cyador (The Saga of Recluce, #10) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Magi'i of Cyador</a>, a glimpse into the history of Toziel &amp; his consort, the emperor of Cyador in Lorn's time.<br /><b>1 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/727699.Magi_i_of_Cyador__The_Saga_of_Recluce___10_" title="Magi'i of Cyador (The Saga of Recluce, #10) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Magi'i of Cyador</a></b> - Year 0 - Lorn must become a Mirror Lancer officer of the White Empire of Cyador, hiding his talents as a magus, while fighting barbarians and the Accursed Forest, and falling in love with the merchanter Ryalth.<br /><b>2 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618245.Scion_of_Cyador__The_Saga_of_Recluce__11_" title="Scion of Cyador (The Saga of Recluce #11) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Scion of Cyador</a></b> - Year 8 - Now an overcaptain, Lorn - and Ryalth - must discover how to keep Lorn from falling prey to plots from ambitious senior officers, merchanters, and Magi'i who plot various coups to take over the Malachite Throne, and stop a barbarian invasion.<br /><b>2.1 - "The Most Successful Merchant"</b> starts before the two Lorn books, is contemporaneous with them, but ends later. <br /><br /><b>3 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185224.Fall_of_Angels__The_Saga_of_Recluce___6_" title="Fall of Angels (The Saga of Recluce, #6) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Fall of Angels</a></b> - Year 401 - Ryba's and Nylan's ship Winterlance breaks the order-chaos barrier into new universe; they and 24 female marines planetfall to the Roof of World, survive local attacks, build Tower Black and Westwind, and begin the Westwind guards.<br /><b>4 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185192.The_Chaos_Balance__The_Saga_of_Recluce__7_" title="The Chaos Balance (The Saga of Recluce #7) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Chaos Balance</a></b> - Year 403 - Nylan and Ayrlyn leave Westwind. They seek refuge in Lornth, which comes under attack by Cyador, the first white empire. Nylan must discover the secret of the accursed forest to save Lornth and his son.<br /><b>4.3 - "Heritage"</b> takes place immediately after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185192.The_Chaos_Balance__The_Saga_of_Recluce__7_" title="The Chaos Balance (The Saga of Recluce #7) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Chaos Balance</a> with the Empress leaving Cyador for new lands.<br /><b>4.5 - The Stranger</b> - begins early in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185224.Fall_of_Angels__The_Saga_of_Recluce___6_" title="Fall of Angels (The Saga of Recluce, #6) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Fall of Angels</a>, but ends several years after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185192.The_Chaos_Balance__The_Saga_of_Recluce__7_" title="The Chaos Balance (The Saga of Recluce #7) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Chaos Balance</a>. It adds to the story of a character who wandered off. Also found in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8459583.Speculative_Horizons" title="Speculative Horizons by Patrick St-Denis" rel="nofollow noopener">Speculative Horizons</a>.<br /><b>5 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6661635.Arms_Commander__The_Saga_of_Recluce___16_" title="Arms-Commander (The Saga of Recluce, #16) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Arms-Commander</a></b> - Year 415 - Saryn and Ryba face invasion of Westwind by Gallos, Suthyan treachery, and a lords' rebellion in Lornth that threatens peace between the Regency and Westwind, and only Saryn can make the difference and pay the price.<br /><br /><b>6 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18490587.Cyador_s_Heirs__The_Saga_of_Recluce___17_" title="Cyador's Heirs (The Saga of Recluce, #17) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Cyador's Heirs</a></b> - Year 425 - Lephi and Lerial, grandsons of the fallen Emperor of Cyador struggle to help their father, Kiedron, maintain the Duchy of Cigoerne, established in Hamor after the fall of Cyad.<br /><b>7 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20518867.Heritage_of_Cyador__The_Saga_of_Recluce___18_" title="Heritage of Cyador (The Saga of Recluce, #18) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Heritage of Cyador</a></b> - Year 433 - Lerial, now a full captain in the Mirror Lancers of Cigoerne, is dispatched to neighboring Afrit to to help repel a possible invasion that threatens not only Afrit, but Cigoerne as well.<br /><br /><b>8 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33517577.The_Mongrel_Mage__The_Saga_of_Recluce___19_" title="The Mongrel Mage (The Saga of Recluce, #19) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Mongrel Mage</a></b> - Year 675 - Beltur is raised as a White wizard, but learns what he really is in Alparata, Spidlar as the Prefect of Gallos is dissatisfied with the status quo. <br /><b>9 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36186983.Outcasts_of_Order__The_Saga_of_Recluce___20_" title="Outcasts of Order (The Saga of Recluce, #20) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Outcasts of Order</a></b> - Year 677 - Beltur discovers he's a frighteningly powerful Order mage &amp; everyone fears or wants to use him.<br /><b>10 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41569618.The_Mage_Fire_War__The_Saga_of_Recluce___21_" title="The Mage-Fire War (The Saga of Recluce, #21) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Mage-Fire War</a></b> From Modesitt's website: <i>I’ve finished the sequel to Outcasts of Order, which will be the third and final book about Beltur [yes, I know it’s the first time I’ve ever written three books about a character in the Saga of Recluce]. It’s entitled The Mage-Fire War, and it’s scheduled for publication and release in July of next year....</i> 9July2018 book released Aug2019<br /><br /><b>10.7 - "Songs Past, Songs for Those to Come"</b> - Year 880 - is a bit about a bard who is often referred to, but rarely shown.<br /><b>11 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185251.The_Towers_of_the_Sunset__The_Saga_of_Recluce__2_" title="The Towers of the Sunset (The Saga of Recluce #2) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Towers of the Sunset</a></b> - Year 900 - Creslin, son of the Marshall of Westwind, flees an arranged marriage; is enslaved by the White Wizards, escapes, and enters a marriage of convenience to Maegara, the white witch; they escape Candar to a desert isle where they create the island nation of Recluce.<br /><b>11.1 - "Sisters of Sarronnyn, Sisters of Westwind"</b> is contemporaneous with above. Also in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1763378.Viewpoints_Critical_Selected_Stories" title="Viewpoints Critical Selected Stories by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Viewpoints Critical: Selected Stories</a>.<br /><br /><b>12 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1123827.The_White_Order__The_Saga_of_Recluce__8_" title="The White Order (The Saga of Recluce #8) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The White Order</a></b> - Year 1190 - Cerryl, orphan son of a renegade white mage, works his way toward the heritage which fate - and the Guild of the White Order - have denied him. He becomes an apprentice scrivener in Fairhaven, only to discover the white wizards are observing his every move... and may take his life.<br /><b>13 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185200.The_Magic_Engineer__The_Saga_of_Recluce__3_" title="The Magic Engineer (The Saga of Recluce #3) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic Engineer</a></b> - Year 1200 - Dorrin is exiled from Recluce because of his love of forbidden machines; he, Kadara, and Brede travel through Candar and settle in Spidlar; the White Wizards of Fairhaven raise mountains and build roads through them to unite Candar under chaos-rule; Dorrin tries to build machines, many turned to war uses by Brede, as the three fend off chaos.<br /><b>13.5 - "Artisan"</b> begins in the early part of<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185200.The_Magic_Engineer__The_Saga_of_Recluce__3_" title="The Magic Engineer (The Saga of Recluce #3) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic Engineer</a> and ends roughly eighteen years after the book ends. Fills in Dorrin's story a bit.<br /><b>14 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/437638.Colors_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__9_" title="Colors of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #9) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Colors of Chaos</a></b> - Year 1205 - Cerryl finds that he had only begun to discover the problems facing Fairhaven and the White Order and now must cope with dangers from all over Candar, from Recluce, and from within Fairhaven itself, including the jealousy and instability of the High Wizard himself.<br /><b>14.3 - "Armsman's Odds"</b> takes place near the end of the above, but the motivation for the story takes place before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1123827.The_White_Order__The_Saga_of_Recluce__8_" title="The White Order (The Saga of Recluce #8) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The White Order</a>. <br /><br /><b>14.6 - "Brass and Lacquer"</b> takes place a hundred-fifty years after the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/437638.Colors_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__9_" title="Colors of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #9) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Colors of Chaos</a>. Set in Recluce with a junior engineer named Talysen.<br /><br /><b>14.9 - "Ice and Fire"</b> is set in the same general time frame as the next book &amp; seems like a good way to segue into it, although it is set in Austra.<br /><b>15 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/437649.Natural_Ordermage__The_Saga_of_Recluce___14_" title="Natural Ordermage (The Saga of Recluce, #14) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Natural Ordermage</a></b> - Year 1500 - Rahl is an apprentice scrivener in Land's End who refuses to believe he has order skills - until he finds himself facing charges of misuse of order and possible exile - or even death - before he is trained and sent to Hamor, where the dangers and challenges he faces are far greater than he realized could be possible.<br /><b>16 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2292175.Mage_Guard_of_Hamor__Saga_of_Recluce___15_" title="Mage-Guard of Hamor (Saga of Recluce, #15) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Mage-Guard of Hamor</a></b> - Year 1503 - As a junior mage-guard, Rahl must return to Recluce with his mentor to tell the magisters of the destruction of their trading center in Swartheld... and then go back to Hamor where he is transferred to the army charged with putting down a rebellion against the Emperor... in a conflict where nothing is what it seems.<br /><br /><b>16.7 - "A Game of Capture"</b> Year 1648 - set in Recluce.<br /><b>17 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185197.The_Order_War__The_Saga_of_Recluce__4_" title="The Order War (The Saga of Recluce #4) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Order War</a></b> - Year 1650 - Justen, a Black engineer, and his brother Gunnar volunteer to help Sarronnyn fight off the White Wizards of Fairhaven; Justen is driven into the Stone Hills, then rescued by a druid to face greater trials. He defies the Council of Recluce and builds a weapon horrifying both the Council and the White Wizards in his efforts to destroy Fairhaven.<br /><b>17.1 "The Price of Perfect Order"</b> is the exception in terms of the chronological order in "Recluce Tales". It takes place around the time of the above, but appears in the book after 'The Assistant Envoy' (17.1).<br /><br /><b>18 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185176.Wellspring_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__12_" title="Wellspring of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #12) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Wellspring of Chaos</a></b> - Year 1710 - Kharl, a cooper in Brysta, rescues a young woman Blackstaffer, only to find that he has earned the wrath of the heir to one of the Lords of the Quadrant who rule Nordla. With a black staff he does not understand and white wizards opposing him he must find a way to leave Brysta or die - yet what of his family and his cooperage?<br /><b>19 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185198.Ordermaster__The_Saga_of_Recluce___13_" title="Ordermaster (The Saga of Recluce, #13) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Ordermaster</a></b> - Year 1712 - Kharl has become the Lord's Mage of Austra, only to find himself facing a rebellion by nobles dissatisfied with Lord Ghrant's efforts to curtail their excesses and corruption. And if he succeeds in keeping the young ruler on the throne, he will face an even greater challenge back in Nordla.<br /><b>19.1 - "The Assistant Envoy's Problem"</b> takes place immediately after the above &amp; features some of the same characters.<br /><br /><b> 19.7 - "Black Ordermage"</b> - Year 1810 - Cassius' origins. Also in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1763378.Viewpoints_Critical_Selected_Stories" title="Viewpoints Critical Selected Stories by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Viewpoints Critical: Selected Stories</a>.<br /><b>20 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce__1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a></b> - Year 1850 - Young, bored, woodworker Lerris leaves Recluce on his dangergeld exile; he travels Candar and finds the gray wizard Justen; he escapes danger and becomes a woodworker again; he fights the great white wizard Antonin; then finds love and understanding with Krystal, subcommander of Kyphros.<br /><b>21 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618243.The_Death_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__5_" title="The Death of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #5) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Chaos</a></b> - Year 1855 - Lerris, Krystal, and all of Candar are threatened by both the growing power of the Emperor of Hamor and the growth of Chaos; Hamor attacks Candar, and then Recluce; in the end Lerris must attempt to destroy Hamor's power and the power of Chaos, or face the proverbial fate worse than death.<br /><b> 21.2 - "Burning Duty"</b> is told some twenty years after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618243.The_Death_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__5_" title="The Death of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #5) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Chaos</a>, but the events take place during the last part of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce__1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a>. Those chairs that were too well made. <br /><b> 21.4 - "Worth"</b> is set just after the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618243.The_Death_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__5_" title="The Death of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #5) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Chaos</a> &amp; cleans up Wrynn's story a bit.<br /><b> 21.6 - "Fame"</b> is set about eighty years after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/618243.The_Death_of_Chaos__The_Saga_of_Recluce__5_" title="The Death of Chaos (The Saga of Recluce #5) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Chaos</a> about how great people are remembered.</span>

<div id="review_56305676" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56305676" />
    <a title="Kara Babcock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1188122-kara-babcock"><img alt="Kara Babcock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580776593p2/1188122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56305676?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara Babcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara Babcock" href="/user/show/1188122-kara-babcock">Kara Babcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=2009-read">2009-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56305676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11045191641377771934">Sometimes I worry I've become too cynical in my old age (says the nineteen-year-old). When I read <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> for the first time, I thought it was the best thing since sliced bread, and I went on to devour the next several books of the Recluce saga before promptly breaking for lunch.... (Well, OK, the span of several months may have elapsed sometime among all that, but you get the idea.) Now I feel less charitable toward this book. <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> has a couple of problems, none of </span>
  <span id="freeText11045191641377771934" style="display:none">Sometimes I worry I've become too cynical in my old age (says the nineteen-year-old). When I read <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> for the first time, I thought it was the best thing since sliced bread, and I went on to devour the next several books of the Recluce saga before promptly breaking for lunch.... (Well, OK, the span of several months may have elapsed sometime among all that, but you get the idea.) Now I feel less charitable toward this book. <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> has a couple of problems, none of them insurmountable and none of them alone detract too much from the story.<br><br>Firstly, the story is slow. This isn't the same as pacing, mind you—the pacing of <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> is a near-perfect balance of dialogue and action sequences. The story is slow because it takes a long time for the main character, Lerris, to develop to a point where we feel invested in him as a person; by the time that happens, the story is nearly over, and suddenly he's fighting the evil wizard. <br><br>Secondly, Lerris seems to suddenly acquire a long-term planning ability that he lacks upon leaving Recluce. He goes from bored youth to concerned woodcrafter, arranging a marriage for his master's daughter and instilling order everywhere. While much of Lerris' maturity can be attributed to character development, I just never got a sense of <i>how</i> Lerris matured, since everyone he meets seems to deplore his idle search for answers.<br><br>Lastly, a good deal of the philosophical discussion in the book is too vague for my liking. I <i>really really</i> love the order/chaos magic system that Modesitt has set up here. However, Justen's (and even Lerris') explanations are too esoteric; I feel like I've landed in an alien university lecture. I get the general gist of the theme that Modesitt wanted to communicate—mainly, that there needs to be balance between order and chaos. However, any serious arguments are stultified by the refusal of those who know better to actually discuss these matters with Lerris. There is a difference between giving someone the answers and debating a point, and the knowledgeable characters of this book seem to confuse the two concepts.<br><br><i>The Magic of Recluce</i> is a highly logistical fantasy novel. By that I mean Modesitt pays close attention to numbers and organization; we get frequent asides that comment on finances, the weather, the political state of the country in which Lerris currently resides, etc. I wouldn't call this a <i>bad</i> thing, but some people might find it boring. Although it would have been nice for Modesitt to develop a slightly more interesting coinage system, and maybe spent less time worrying about coin and more about work in general (Lerris never could seem to dabble in anything; once he tried to do something, he went at it full bore), I didn't mind the logistical elements. It gave me some time to mull over the vagueness surrounding order/chaos theory.<br><br>As far as characterization goes, I honestly didn't pay attention to any of the characters except for the few main ones. It seems that Lerris met the same hostile innkeeper at every village (and subsequently had to make a hasty escape from said inn). Even the arguably main characters, however, don't feel very real. Modesitt fails to provide us with any explanation for their inner conflicts. Krystal clearly has issues, but what are they? What really happened in Justen's past? Even more hints or veiled implications would be better than absolute ignorance, the result of which was my apathy toward Krystal's attraction to Lerris and Justen's attitude at the end of the book.<br><br>In the end, <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> adheres too faithfully to the standard fantasy tropes. It is technically sound, much like a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8732.David_Eddings" title="David Eddings" rel="nofollow noopener">David Eddings</a> novel, but lacks the truly intriguing hook to make it amazing. Hopefully my memory will be correct in that the later books in this series are far better, especially when it comes to the quality of the characters. I do recall not feeling as passionate about <i>The Magic of Recluce</i> as I did about its successors, re-reading it only because it's the first book. We'll see how I like the next ones.<br><br><strong>My reviews of the <em>Recluce saga</em>:</strong><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67617044" rel="nofollow noopener"><em>The Towers of Sunset</em> →</a><br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc/3.0/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons License" width="88" height="31" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238653i/681550.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11045191641377771934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3338669683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3338669683" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3338669683?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3338669683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093701959963660977">As I was reading, I kept having to stop and convince myself that I wasn't reading a book that came out in the last few years. It's style and worldbuilding and quick developments belied the fact that it was pubbed in 1991. And yet?<br/><br/>I was entranced. I felt like I was reading Robin Hobb (this came out before her popular epic fantasy) mixed with some Robert Jordan and some of the high-fantasy elements of Moorcock.<br/><br/>And it wasn't even the magic dichotomy between Order vs Chaos and how it felt like a gig</span>
  <span id="freeText17093701959963660977" style="display:none">As I was reading, I kept having to stop and convince myself that I wasn't reading a book that came out in the last few years. It's style and worldbuilding and quick developments belied the fact that it was pubbed in 1991. And yet?<br /><br />I was entranced. I felt like I was reading Robin Hobb (this came out before her popular epic fantasy) mixed with some Robert Jordan and some of the high-fantasy elements of Moorcock.<br /><br />And it wasn't even the magic dichotomy between Order vs Chaos and how it felt like a gigantic Yin/Yang motif that got me revved up. It wasn't even the interesting feel of reading LeGuin's fantasy tucked away in these pages.<br /><br />It was the Main Character. <br /><br />I've never seen the ultimate growth of a wet-nosed teen to a magician of the high order come packaged in such a MODEST package. <br /><br />I'll be frank. The main character charmed me the most.<br /><br />I love the magic system and learning how it worked and following his long discoveries was fantastic, but it was his personality that made me love this book. :)<br /><br />I'm definitely going to continue this series. I had a misstep with one of his other, later books, but if I had started here, I never would have worried. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17093701959963660977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fantasy">sci-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=unforgivable-cover-art">unforgivable-cover-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127417056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17161162725793240738">There are three reasons why I love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce___1_' title='The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce, #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr.' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Magic of Recluce</a>: 1) it's not like the Star Wars movies in one crucial way; 2) it is built around training rather than adventure; 3) woodworking.<br/><br/><u>1) Not Star Wars:</u> There is a line in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77111.The_Empire_Strikes_Back__Star_Wars___5_' title='The Empire Strikes Back (Star Wars, #5) by Donald F. Glut' rel='nofollow noopener'>Empire Strikes Back</a> where Yoda says, "A Jedi uses the Force for knowledge and defense, NEVER for attack." There is no equivocation in that. It is NEVER for attack. Pretty simple, I would think. Yet the movies are packed with our Jedis on the offensive, including Yoda in the preq</span>
  <span id="freeText17161162725793240738" style="display:none">There are three reasons why I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce___1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce, #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a>: 1) it's not like the Star Wars movies in one crucial way; 2) it is built around training rather than adventure; 3) woodworking.<br /><br /><u>1) Not Star Wars:</u> There is a line in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77111.The_Empire_Strikes_Back__Star_Wars___5_" title="The Empire Strikes Back (Star Wars, #5) by Donald F. Glut" rel="nofollow noopener">Empire Strikes Back</a> where Yoda says, "A Jedi uses the Force for knowledge and defense, NEVER for attack." There is no equivocation in that. It is NEVER for attack. Pretty simple, I would think. Yet the movies are packed with our Jedis on the offensive, including Yoda in the prequels. I wanted to believe Yoda. I wanted it to be true. I wanted Luke's confrontation with Darth Vader in Bespin to be as much a mistake because of its offensive nature as it was a mistake of his youth.<br /><br />I've debated and discussed this with many over the years, and one of the most frustrating excuses for the movies is that "there is no other way." I've always argued that there is another way, and that the failure to embrace that other way is a terrible failure of the films and its creator (I am fine with using the violence of attack as an answer, so long as the great guru of our hero doesn't say that it is NEVER for attack). But my argument has been written off as mere theory because while I have argued that there is another way all I had was my assertion that there was. Now I have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce___1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce, #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a>. Where Lucas fails, Modesitt Jr. succeeds. Where Luke Skywalker fails, Lerris succeeds. Where the flawed use of force fails, order succeeds by letting chaos destroy itself. <br /><br />Lerris doesn't need big weapons. He actually breaks his own staff at one point and uses a shield as his "weapon." Lerris spends the novel disarming people, avoiding people, protecting people and attempting to bring order to the chaos around him. And there is no loss of excitement in the story. Big action be damned.<br /><br /><u>2) Training:</u> I am a big sucker for training stories. It has always been one of my favourite aspects of war movies (raw recruits becoming soldiers), martial arts movies (ninja and samurai mastering their weapons), and sports movies (especially the crappy baseball team going back to basics). I suppose it is because I like to learn and I like to teach, but it is also a wonderful tool of storytelling because it breathes life into characters very naturally. Character development must happen. There is no avoiding it when a character's <i>raison d'etre</i> is to change. And here, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce___1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce, #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a>, Lerris is learning from the first page to the last, even when he is bored, even when he is seeking, even when he is teaching and even when he is just riding his pony. Lerris learns and that is good.<br /><br /><u>3) Woodworking:</u> This may seem like an odd reason for loving the story, but the woodworking is quite a beautiful addition to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce___1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce, #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a>. It grounds our hero, is key to his search for his place in order and chaos, links him permanently to the land of his birth and provides him with an occupation when times get tight. And it is the latter economic use of woodworking that I liked best. <br /><br />Fantasy novels and their characters rarely worry themselves with anything as mundane as money. Even the poorest farmboy turned hero just goes out in the world and has everything happen for him. There is some early testing adventure that puts him in danger, and when he walks away from it he has a full purse and food just falls into his lap whenever he needs it (either because he is an accomplished hunter or everyone's happy to give their food away). Not for Lerris. He makes his way through the Easthorns after a last ditch escape from Jellico and finds himself short on food and short on funds. So what does he do? He gets himself a gig as a journeyman woodworker and spends a good third of the novel becoming a master builder. This, of course, does much more for him than simply providing money (it is probably the most important part of his personal training), but to see a hero concerned with the day to day difficulties of living pushed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/185253.The_Magic_of_Recluce__The_Saga_of_Recluce___1_" title="The Magic of Recluce (The Saga of Recluce, #1) by L.E. Modesitt Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic of Recluce</a> into rarified air for me. <br /><br />It is a damn good novel, but the woodworking? The woodworking makes it great. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17161162725793240738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_71001239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71001239" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71001239?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/8555161-the-magic-of-recluce">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=scifi-fan-group">scifi-fan-group</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71001239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12555088628712516332">An engaging read that starts out as a coming-of-age fantasy and advances into something...else. It reminds me in places of Robert Jordan, Michael Moorcock, and Steven Erikson, yet has its own voice.<br/><br/>Modesitt gets a high score for his world building. The world of Recluce is wonderful and the surface is only scratched at here. I'm intrigued enough by this to read more in the series at some point. Since all but one of the 15 or so other books out there happen before this one, there's plenty of backs</span>
  <span id="freeText12555088628712516332" style="display:none">An engaging read that starts out as a coming-of-age fantasy and advances into something...else. It reminds me in places of Robert Jordan, Michael Moorcock, and Steven Erikson, yet has its own voice.<br /><br />Modesitt gets a high score for his world building. The world of Recluce is wonderful and the surface is only scratched at here. I'm intrigued enough by this to read more in the series at some point. Since all but one of the 15 or so other books out there happen before this one, there's plenty of backstory to add to the world here.<br /><br />I also enjoyed Modesitt's pace and style. He uses the first person narrative style as the story is revealed by the main character, Lerris. He's a young man learning his powers and his way in the world. He seems to start out as a typical Rand/Frodo/Richard Cypher/Luke Skywalker type but eventually matures into an interesting character in his own right. And he does this mostly by learning things for himself, rather than having a Gandalf figure to tell him what to do.<br /><br />The magic system of Recluce is excellent. Basically, all of the magic is centered around the forces of order and chaos, and the manipulation or of keeping them up. This is where the Moorcock reminders are. I enjoyed seeing Lerris learn about the system and seeing it in practice from him and others utilizing it. The chaos-masters and order-masters, commanding the white of chaos and black of order fascinated me. I love the switch from typical by having white reprsent evil and black for good, though they're not quite as black and white (forgive the play on words) as that. Chaos leads to evil but isn't evil in and of itself. Same thing with order. The relationships and manipulations of chaos and order are what end up defining good and evil here.<br /><br />There are some small breaks in the course of the novel where the author switches to a present tense third person and gives us hints as to other happenings away from Lerris. I had mixed feelings about those. While they were interesting and helped set up some of the big picture drama, they were too few and far between to really help the story that much. They were also pretty vague and honestly took away from some of the surprise later. It was a jolt in the narrative whenever one of these came up, both to switch into the third person and then back to Lerris's view. In my opinion, they should have been left out. Or, where there was something useful there, maybe it could have been told to Lerris by someone on the road. As far as giving the reader something that Lerris didn't know, that doesn't make sense in a first person story. There was a LOT going on that he didn't pick up all the details on, and that was fine. It added to the mystery of the world and story.<br /><br />The other annoying thing wasn't as minor. In fact, it bugged the piss out of me and might have helped keep this book from a 5-star rating. The f**king sound effects! That was a narrative flaw that could very well get a book tossed into the burn pile. If this story wasn't as engaging as it was, that would have had me heading right back to the library to drop this thing in the overnight return.<br /><br />Here's an example:<br /><br />"<i>Tharoom...thud...tharoom...</i> Walking the white fir was walking across a massive drum. Antonin's coach must have vied with the real thunder when it rumbled across his bridge...<i>Tharummmm...<br />Creaaakkkk...</i>The heavy wooden gate, set on massive bronze hinges, eased open even more widely as I watched."<br /><br />That's annoying. I felt like I was watching one of those old cheesy Batman television episodes. There are ways to describe sound without treating the reader like an idiot or make them feel like they're reading a comic book without pictures. Luckily he didn't really get rolling with this technique too early in the book, and by the time he did I was already hooked by the story. Otherwise it would have been "holy cheesy effects, Batman" and I would have moved on to something else. I was able to live with them eventually, my eyes blurring over and past to the real narrative beyond.<br /><br />Overall, I give this book high points for the world building, the magic system, the characters, and the writing voice used by Modesitt over the course of <i>most</i> of the novel. I'm definitely interested in reading more books in the Recluce series, I'm just hoping he cuts back on the special effects.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12555088628712516332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2068732710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068732710" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2068732710?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33023712-the-magic-of-recluce">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2068732710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17319667641177710447">Usually in the field of high fantasy I choose recent works, but I like to look for the distant and the near past for corresponding works Phase difference have influenced The current writers. One of these works is this book, which starts a very large set of books that continues even nowadays, so we can say that it is at the same time recent.<br/><br/>In this first book, therefore, we start from a utopian place where order and stability reign, tensions are non-existent and, in general, its inhabitants live </span>
  <span id="freeText17319667641177710447" style="display:none">Usually in the field of high fantasy I choose recent works, but I like to look for the distant and the near past for corresponding works Phase difference have influenced The current writers. One of these works is this book, which starts a very large set of books that continues even nowadays, so we can say that it is at the same time recent.<br /><br />In this first book, therefore, we start from a utopian place where order and stability reign, tensions are non-existent and, in general, its inhabitants live a peaceful life. To do this, however, the authorities manage creatively those people find this whole order boring and want to do more. This creative management involves exile to other parts of the world where they are called upon to find their way but also to help stabilize these areas where they are sent.<br /><br />One of them is our young hero who is bored with the life that has set him up and wants to make something more exciting. So, after a short period of learning, they send him along with others to a nearby area where things are more... chaotic, as various competitions and power games have led to a lasting war. Here our hero - like his friends - is called upon to mature, cultivate more his magic powers and be able to bring peace to this region. But quickly he understands that things are very difficult, as against him are the magical powers of chaos that threaten to destroy everything and then spread their influence across the globe. To face this evil needs to make difficult choices that even in the end can not know if they are right.<br /><br />That is how this series begins, with a book in which the reader will not find much action or very intense emotions but will find different things that may be even more essential as the author focuses more on our hero and on his personal quest, inviting us to identify with him, comparing our own search with his own. So we follow its course which leads us to an interesting story, although in some places this interest is diminishing, while at a time the rather subdued finale does not offer complete satisfaction. At the same time, however, the author puts out several philosophical questions, insisting much on the contrast between order and chaos, which the more learned know is at the core of the perceptions of every human civilization. Of course, this philosophical search is somewhat simplistic and does not reach much depth, but it is capable of putting the reader in thought and this is quite important and makes me appreciate what I read.<br /><br />Συνήθως στο χώρο της υψηλής φαντασίας επιλέγω πρόσφατα έργα, μου αρέσει, όμως, να ψάχνω στο μακρινό και το κοντινό παρελθόν για αντίστοιχα έργα διαφορά φάσης έχουν επηρεάσει Τους σημερινούς συγγραφείς. Ένα από αυτά τα έργα είναι αυτό εδώ το βιβλίο, το οποίο ξεκινάει μία ιδιαίτερα μεγάλη σειρά βιβλίων που συνεχίζεται ακόμα και στις μέρες μας, οπότε μπορούμε να πούμε ότι είναι και σημερινή ταυτόχρονα.<br /><br />Σε αυτό το πρώτο βιβλίο, λοιπόν, ξεκινάμε από ένα ουτοπικό μέρος, όπου βασιλεύει η τάξη και η σταθερότητα, οι εντάσεις είναι ανύπαρκτες και γενικότερα οι κάτοικοι του ζούνε μία ειρηνική ζωή. Για να το επιτύχουν αυτό, όμως, οι αρχές διαχειρίζονται δημιουργικά εκείνα τα άτομα βρίσκουν όλη αυτή την τάξη βαρετή και θέλουν να κάνουν κάτι περισσότερο. Αυτή η δημιουργική διαχείριση περιλαμβάνει την εξορία τους σε άλλα μέρη του πλανήτη όπου εκεί καλούνται να βρουν το δρόμο τους αλλά και να βοηθήσουν στην σταθεροποίηση αυτών των περιοχών όπου αποστέλλονται.<br /><br />Ένας από αυτούς είναι ο νεαρός ήρωάς μας που βαριέται αφόρητα τη ζωή που το έχουν ορίσει και ζητάει να κάνει κάτι συναρπαστικότερο. Έτσι, μετά από μία σύντομη περίοδο εκπαίδευσης, τον στέλνουν μαζί με κάποιους άλλους σε μία κοντινή περιοχή όπου τα πράγματα είναι περισσότερο... χαοτικά, καθώς oi διάφοροι ανταγωνισμοί και τα παιχνίδια εξουσίας έχουν οδηγήσει σε μία διαρκή εμπόλεμη κατάσταση. Εκεί ο ήρωάς μας - όπως και οι φίλοι του - καλείται να ωριμάσει, να καλλιεργήσει περισσότερο τις μαγικές του δυνάμεις και να μπορέσει να φέρει την ειρήνη σε αυτήν την περιοχή. Γρήγορα, όμως, καταλαβαίνεις ότι τα πράγματα είναι πολύ δύσκολα καθώς απέναντί του βρίσκονται οι μαγικές δυνάμεις του χάους που απειλούν να καταστρέψουν τα πάντα και μετά να εξαπλώσουν την επιρροή τους σε ολόκληρο τον πλανήτη. Για να αντιμετωπίσει αυτό το κακό χρειάζεται να κάνει δύσκολες επιλογές που ακόμα και στο τέλος δεν μπορεί να ξέρει αν είναι σωστές.<br /><br />Κάπως έτσι ξεκινάει αυτή η σειρά, με ένα βιβλίο στο οποίο ο αναγνώστης δεν θα βρει πολύ δράση ή πολύ έντονες συγκινήσεις, θα βρει, όμως, διαφορετικά πράγματα που ίσως είναι και πιο ουσιαστικά καθώς ο συγγραφέας επικεντρώνεται περισσότερο στον ήρωά μας και στην προσωπική αναζήτηση του, καλώντας μας ίσως να ταυτιστούμε μαζί του, συγκρίνοντας τη δική μας αναζήτηση με τη δική του. Έτσι παρακολουθούμε την πορεία του η οποία μας οδηγεί σε μία ενδιαφέρουσα ιστορία, αν και σε κάποια σημεία αυτό το ενδιαφέρον μειώνεται, τη στιγμή που το μάλλον κάπως υποτονικό φινάλε δεν προσφέρει απόλυτη ικανοποίηση. Παράλληλα, όμως, ο συγγραφέας βάζει και αρκετά φιλοσοφικά ερωτήματα, επιμένοντας πολύ στην αντίθεση μεταξύ της τάξης και του χάους, κάτι που οι περισσότεροι διαβασμένοι γνωρίζουν ότι είναι στον πυρήνα των αντιλήψεων κάθε ανθρώπινου πολιτισμού. Βέβαια αυτή η φιλοσοφική αναζήτηση είναι κάπως απλοϊκή και δεν φτάνει σε μεγάλο βάθος, είναι ικανή, όμως, να βάλει τον αναγνώστη σε σκέψη και αυτό είναι αρκετά σημαντικό και με κάνει να εκτιμώ αυτό που διάβασα.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17319667641177710447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24181235" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24181235" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/899665-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375036866p2/899665.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24181235?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/899665-jon">Jon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jon by: </span>
      SF/Fantasy Book Club November 2010 Selection
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=read-in-my-30s">read-in-my-30s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=read-in-my-40s">read-in-my-40s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=read-in-my-20s">read-in-my-20s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24181235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15127167580466293218">Excellent world building and superb magic system with an annoyingly dense but affable young adult protagonist on a quest. Lerris is 'the chosen one' but for all the wrong reasons or completely mysterious hidden reasons until he's painted himself into a corner with his fumbling choices. Lerris isn't burdened with a prophecy, but he resists the status quo of Recluce. Lerris is just your typical young adult with attention deficit disorder (i.e., he's bored and finds everything boring), but Recluce </span>
  <span id="freeText15127167580466293218" style="display:none">Excellent world building and superb magic system with an annoyingly dense but affable young adult protagonist on a quest. Lerris is 'the chosen one' but for all the wrong reasons or completely mysterious hidden reasons until he's painted himself into a corner with his fumbling choices. Lerris isn't burdened with a prophecy, but he resists the status quo of Recluce. Lerris is just your typical young adult with attention deficit disorder (i.e., he's bored and finds everything boring), but Recluce doesn't prescribe Ritalin. Somewhat like extreme Amish, Recluce peacefully forces their misfits to either exile permanently or go on dangergeld (similar to rumspringa but with a quest attached), during which they must decide if they can return to Recluce and succumb to its creed and worldview (seeking perfection in Order). This novel follows Lerris on his journey as a dangergelder until he understands all that Recluce embodies and effects, and reaches his decision. <br /><br />If you are looking for a story with character growth, Lerris' journey as an exile from Recluce will fit that bill. If you are looking for a new fantasy world with a detailed history, divergent societies, a logical robust magic system, with a different spin on the age-old struggle between angels and demons, good and evil, black and white, order and chaos, then you've come to the right story and series. <br /><br />Modesitt's Recluce series reminds me of Asimov's robot stories. He sets up a scenario with some basic, seemingly simple rules (for example, Asimov's Three Laws of Robotics and Modesitt's Order/Chaos balance system as glimpsed through snippets of <i>The Basis of Order</i>) and proceeds to challenge those rules with his world and its characters. While each novel adds a piece of the broader puzzle, for the most part, like this first one, the books stand alone quite well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15127167580466293218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nils | nilsreviewsit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nils | nilsreviewsit" href="/user/show/52846007-nils-nilsreviewsit">Nils | nilsreviewsit</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2131446538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13249134303645254720">I'm sorry to say that this book was a DNF for me! I'm so disappointed that I didn't like this one, I really tried to give it a fair go, and I read about halfway through, but to be honest it was stressing me out and I had to leave it!<br/><br/>It wasn't all negative as I really did enjoy the beginning of the book. The Magic of Recluce is written in first person, and the downfall of this narration can be that it makes a book lack world building. There was none of that here! Modesitt showed himself to be ski</span>
  <span id="freeText13249134303645254720" style="display:none">I'm sorry to say that this book was a DNF for me! I'm so disappointed that I didn't like this one, I really tried to give it a fair go, and I read about halfway through, but to be honest it was stressing me out and I had to leave it!<br /><br />It wasn't all negative as I really did enjoy the beginning of the book. The Magic of Recluce is written in first person, and the downfall of this narration can be that it makes a book lack world building. There was none of that here! Modesitt showed himself to be skilled at world building and really weaved in beautiful details of culture and scenery into the narrative. I mean the food that was described left my mouth watering!<br /><br />The main issue for me was that I really disliked the main character, Lerris. From the very beginning he does not stop moaning about everything. He finds everything boring and annoying. He constantly complained, mostly because he was never given any answers and wanted everything told to him, okay at times this was a valid reason, but it was still so frustrating to read. It actually made me bored! I know that later on Lerris does improve, but by then I really didn't care.<br /><br />Another one of my biggest problems was that Modesitt used sound effects to describe things. He would use phrases like 'thwack' for fight scenes and 'wheeee eeee' to describe the sound of a horse!! My God did this piss me off! I mean it was one 'kapow' away from being like a 60s Batman tv episode! Not good! If you're going to give me a battle scene, give me the details, give me a scene to visualise. Don't give me a 'thwack' and bits of broken up conversation!<br /><br />Anyway I'm still glad I tried a new author, I mean you don't know until you try right?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13249134303645254720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
