<div id="review_264697579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264697579" />
    <a title="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1497559-jayaprakash-satyamurthy"><img alt="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517076488p2/1497559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264697579?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jayaprakash Satyamurthy" href="/user/show/1497559-jayaprakash-satyamurthy">Jayaprakash Satyamurthy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857232011" href="/book/show/437643.The_Magic_of_Recluce">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497559-jayaprakash-satyamurthy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264697579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9543167361894390255">This isn't pathbreaking fantasy, and it suffers from issues of pacing, prose and characterisation, but it's an engaging and sometimes moving story for all that. <br/><br/>A coming of age novel set in a fantastic world (aren't they all?), The Magic Of Recluce often seems bogged down in diurnal detail: meals at inns, distances travelled, long hours of discomfort, but I can also see how Modesitt felt the need to include these things as a way to ground his fantasy narrative, give it a lived-in feel. The prose</span>
  <span id="freeText9543167361894390255" style="display:none">This isn't pathbreaking fantasy, and it suffers from issues of pacing, prose and characterisation, but it's an engaging and sometimes moving story for all that. <br /><br />A coming of age novel set in a fantastic world (aren't they all?), The Magic Of Recluce often seems bogged down in diurnal detail: meals at inns, distances travelled, long hours of discomfort, but I can also see how Modesitt felt the need to include these things as a way to ground his fantasy narrative, give it a lived-in feel. The prose itself is serviceable, but ever so slightly awkward. Sometimes it's hard to tell exactly which character is being referred to, or who just spoke and Modessit's reliance on onomatopoeia to convey action can get tiresome as well as opaque. The characters are broad archetypes to the point of cliche, but Modesitt goes beyond the traditional gender roles of a lot of fantasy.<br /><br />Despite the fact that things often move too slowly for the narrative's good, the plot is actually very well shaped and highly effective, setting up a central conflict and then successively raising the stakes, along with interludes to gather energy. It all builds up to a magnificent sorcercous confrontation in a forbidden castle - pure fantasy overdrive. Along the way, we're exposed to complex and compelling political currents and an interesting, nuanced conception of magic. <br /><br />This book also features the single most awesome pony in all of fantastic fiction.<br /><br />So there you go: a middling epic fantasy novel that offers an interesting take on magic, a richly imagined world, a predictable but exciting plot, some infelicities of style and a certain shallowness of charaterisation. Quite a few rungs above Eddings and certainly more genuinely imaginative and original than Jordan. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9543167361894390255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_724383592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724383592" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/724383592?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=z-1990s">z-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=interlibrary-loan">interlibrary-loan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724383592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4753593584413466488">I liked this book well enough, but it really didn’t distinguish itself. Young Lerris gets sent off to do what is called dangergeld because he is bored with his perfect, utopian life. As per usual in this kind of story, he discovers that he has talents he never suspected, that his parents aren’t who he thought they were, and that non-utopian life can be rather difficult. You know, the usual in these fantasy epics. (See <i>The Belgariad</i> by David Eddings, <i>The Riftwar Saga</i> by Raymond Feist, or <i>Memory, </i></span>
  <span id="freeText4753593584413466488" style="display:none">I liked this book well enough, but it really didn’t distinguish itself. Young Lerris gets sent off to do what is called dangergeld because he is bored with his perfect, utopian life. As per usual in this kind of story, he discovers that he has talents he never suspected, that his parents aren’t who he thought they were, and that non-utopian life can be rather difficult. You know, the usual in these fantasy epics. (See <i>The Belgariad</i> by David Eddings, <i>The Riftwar Saga</i> by Raymond Feist, or <i>Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn</i> by Tad Williams or even the King Arthur legend).<br /><br />There is some attempt made to produce meaningful female characters, but unfortunately they are only there as foils and props for Lerris. When he needs someone to bring him down a peg or two, there’s Tamra. When he needs a romantic interest, there’s Krystal. But they retreat into obscurity when they are not needed for some plot point. It’s nice that they’re intelligent and talented, but they don’t get to shine, at least in this first book. They don’t even really talk to one another, except to discuss Lerris a little bit.<br /><br />I’ve cheated a bit and peeked at the Wikipedia entry for this series—if that’s accurate, I have some hope for the series. Two technologically advanced cultures are marooned on this world and have very different world views. That reminds me of Julian May’s <i>Saga of Pliocene Exile</i> enough to pique my curiosity and send me looking for at least the second book in the series. <br /><br /><b>Book number 282 in my Science Fiction and Fantasy Reading Project.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4753593584413466488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15390755519056369318">I first read this over 25 years ago & it hooked me on the Recluce series. It's the first published, but 17th in the chronology (C17, P01). It was a real journey of discovery that first time as Modesitt built the complicated world through Lerris' eyes, a young, disaffected man who was ignorant of so much. My one real issue with the book is how much he suddenly understood toward the end. I guess he's a lot smarter than I am.<br/><br/>My favorite parts were the woodworking & the horse (large pony). I'm a woo</span>
  <span id="freeText15390755519056369318" style="display:none">I first read this over 25 years ago &amp; it hooked me on the Recluce series. It's the first published, but 17th in the chronology (C17, P01). It was a real journey of discovery that first time as Modesitt built the complicated world through Lerris' eyes, a young, disaffected man who was ignorant of so much. My one real issue with the book is how much he suddenly understood toward the end. I guess he's a lot smarter than I am.<br /><br />My favorite parts were the woodworking &amp; the horse (large pony). I'm a woodworker &amp;, if it isn't obvious from my profile picture, ride a large pony of my own &amp; even use a hackamore on him. Both require a lot of work that is generally ignored by authors. There were some obvious oversights in both, but Modesitt does a far better job than most &amp; at least he tried hard.<br /><br />IMO, this book reads a lot better in chronological order than published order. The whole series does. For a list of the current chronology of this series, see my review here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30803131">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11383871068996171695">Not quite 3.5 stars. <br/><br/>I didn’t know what to expect going into this book. I knew it was the first of a long series and the ratings/reviews had me wondering. The pace of the book is pretty slow. It involves a lot of daily life type of descriptions.   <span id="freeText11383871068996171695" style="display:none">Not quite 3.5 stars. <br /><br />I didn’t know what to expect going into this book. I knew it was the first of a long series and the ratings/reviews had me wondering. The pace of the book is pretty slow. It involves a lot of daily life type of descriptions. I thought that this would make me lose interest. There were times that I felt this everyday life events could have been shorted to move the book along, but overall I came to enjoy it. It felt comfortable to me and relaxing, which I wasn’t expecting. The book did have exciting parts also. I enjoyed the character development and felt that I got to know them well. The magic system was interesting and refreshing from a lot of other fantasy novels. I enjoyed the writing style of the author. The book flowed well and was easy to read. I will continue in the future with this series to see how it evolves. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_9117239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9117239" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/316799-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196198918p2/316799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9117239?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/316799-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy aficionados</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/316799-mark?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9117239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1461092419012427625">"The Magic of Recluce" is the first book in L.E. Modesitt's long-running "Recluce" saga. This series has grown to encompass 14 books.<br/><br/>The denizens of Modesitt's world are all human beings. The magic system of this world is based on order and chaos. Chaos wizards enhance the chaos in people and things while order wizards enhance the order in people and things. Chaos is classified as an "evil" magic and order as a "good" magic. It's a pretty cool and logical system, although I was disappointed that</span>
  <span id="freeText1461092419012427625" style="display:none">"The Magic of Recluce" is the first book in L.E. Modesitt's long-running "Recluce" saga. This series has grown to encompass 14 books.<br /><br />The denizens of Modesitt's world are all human beings. The magic system of this world is based on order and chaos. Chaos wizards enhance the chaos in people and things while order wizards enhance the order in people and things. Chaos is classified as an "evil" magic and order as a "good" magic. It's a pretty cool and logical system, although I was disappointed that each branch of magic had a morality attached to it. To me, it would seem that the magics themselves would be amoral, and the morality of their use dependent upon the individual using the magic, with a balance between order and chaos being the preferred, happy medium.<br /><br />The Plot<br />Recluce is an island nation consisting of order wizards and those who live under their rule. Citizens who are dissatisfied with this order in any way have two choices: Exile or Dangergeld. <br /><br />Lerris, our protagonist, decides on a dangergeld, which is a form of public service where a citizen is trained to survive in the world outside Recluce and then sent on some kind of mission. Presumably, while performing this mission, the dangergelder will come to find his or her place in the world and come back to Recluce, or find a spot in the outside world to live after the mission is accomplished.<br /><br />Lerris gets trained, leaves Recluce, and the fun begins.<br /><br />The Good<br />As stated before, the magic system is logical and cool: Order magic is more focused on strengthening that which already exists and Chaos magic is more focused on weakening existing things.<br /><br />Other reviews have said that the story keeping track of the character's money and their financial struggles was dull. However, I liked this aspect of it. Too often, stories depict square-jawed heroes venturing forth with no consideration as to the financial or logistical elements of such a journey. Either the protagonist is independently wealthy or the author just doesn't write about how a character lives day to day. In the Recluce novels, the characters have to work to survive.<br /><br />I liked how Modesitt would change writing styles during the story. When Lerris, the protagonist, is narrating, Modesitt writes in first person past tense ("I walked down the muddy road"). When scenes without Lerris occur in the story, Modesitt changes to third person present tense ("She walks down the muddy road"). I thought this was really cool and original.<br /><br />The Bad<br />I didn't like that Order was equated with good and Chaos was equated with bad. I prefer the morality of magic being determined by the person using it. In order for the world to work properly, it seems to me that both Order and Chaos is needed, working in a kind of balance; not only in the world, but in an individual as well. <br /><br />The novel kind of addresses this, but not really to my satisfaction.<br /><br />Another place the novel falls flat are the characters. The only really compelling character is Lerris, the protagonist, which is certainly a good thing. The other notable characters were the antagonist and the gray wizard, Justen. Pretty much all of the other characters seemed to meld together and it was difficult to tell one from another.<br /><br />Conclusion<br />If you are an avid fantasy novel reader, you should check the Recluce series out. It's not the "flash bang" of the more popular series out there, but it is an entertaining read.<br /><br />I wouldn't recommend the Recluce novels to dabblers in fantasy reading, or to those looking for a gateway into fantasy literature. There are parts of this novel that are just too dry.<br /><br />If you're looking for your next fantasy fix, though, I say try out the first novel. If it's to your liking, you may want to try the rest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1461092419012427625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_110695039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110695039" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480301169p2/2517340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110695039?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110695039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2701771155149063239">This was an enjoyable read. Nothing spectacular, definitely not five stars for me, but it could have at least been four stars if not for one very annoying component... But more on that later.<br/><br/>The characters - I liked them. Some of the relationships that formed between them seemed a little unbelievable and/or unnatural to me, but it wasn't so bad as to interfere with my enjoyment of the story. The magic system - interesting, I liked the idea of order versus chaos and all of the rules that went wit</span>
  <span id="freeText2701771155149063239" style="display:none">This was an enjoyable read. Nothing spectacular, definitely not five stars for me, but it could have at least been four stars if not for one very annoying component... But more on that later.<br /><br />The characters - I liked them. Some of the relationships that formed between them seemed a little unbelievable and/or unnatural to me, but it wasn't so bad as to interfere with my enjoyment of the story. The magic system - interesting, I liked the idea of order versus chaos and all of the rules that went with each side. The world was also interesting to me, I found myself wanting to keep reading so that I could learn more about Recluce and unravel the mysteries surrounding it. The plot was sort of so so.. Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed reading it.. But for most of the book it just sort of meandered along. The plot was advancing, but I had no idea what it was advancing towards. It only really started coming together and wrapping up in the last third or quarter. But like I said - the ride to get there was interesting, I just would have liked some more hints as to what the overall plot was a little earlier on.<br /><br />Now back to the annoying component.. The sound effects. What the heck was up with those sound effects? They were so awkward and out of place in the story! Some examples of what I mean...<br /><br /><i>Thwup, thwup, thwup... thwup, thwup, thwup... The paddles churned, dipping into the water with increasing speed, and a heavier and thicker plume of whitish smoke billowed from the stack.<br /><br />... clink... clink... clunk... Sweat was pouring from his face, and he was breathing hard.... clink... clunk... Crack!... Whsssttt... "Aiiieee...!" Clank..<br /><br />Thrummmm... thrumm... Splatt... splattt... The cold raindrops on my head prompted me to complete my recovery of the cloak and to replace the pack behind the saddle.</i><br /><br />Seriously.. What is up with that? They are completely unnecessary, annoying, and <i>everywhere</i>. They didn't really show up right away, which is good because I probably would have dropped the book right away if they had. By the time they did show up I was already interested in the story, so I pushed through. But seriously.. They almost ruin the story. <br /><br />So overall - the story/characters/magic/world in general gets four stars, but I have to take off a star for the sound effects. I will likely read on in the series, but I'm definitely keeping my fingers crossed that the sound effects go away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2701771155149063239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_93466348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93466348" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/867629-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404333616p2/867629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93466348?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/867629-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867629-justin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93466348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer99432520391665578">Bleh. Technically I shouldn't mark this as "read," since I've only made it through about 175 pages or so.<br/><br/>I've seen these books praised by fantasy readers, and am lucky enough to have a set signed by the author. But I can't really see the appeal. This is a book in dire need of a more merciless editor. It's turgid past the point of forgiveness. Everything moves so. Slow. That. I. Find. Myself. Not. Giving. A. Damn.<br/><br/>Modesitt takes great care to describe each room his characters enter in excruciating</span>
  <span id="freeText99432520391665578" style="display:none">Bleh. Technically I shouldn't mark this as "read," since I've only made it through about 175 pages or so.<br /><br />I've seen these books praised by fantasy readers, and am lucky enough to have a set signed by the author. But I can't really see the appeal. This is a book in dire need of a more merciless editor. It's turgid past the point of forgiveness. Everything moves so. Slow. That. I. Find. Myself. Not. Giving. A. Damn.<br /><br />Modesitt takes great care to describe each room his characters enter in excruciating detail, down to the grain of the floorboards. But the descriptive language doesn't stop there; we also get detailed breakdowns of lunches, ablutions, and aimless wanderings. Conversations of no particular importance are faithfully recorded, even if they don't consist of anything but some "oh"s, "well"s, a few ellipses, and some onomatopoeia. Which wouldn't be so bad if any of the characters were likable, but sadly, with one exception (Sammel) they are all extremely irritating. Especially Lerris. See, here's the thing: if the main character is bored and annoyed all the time for no particular reason, it makes for a pretty boring and annoying read that doesn't seem to be going in any particular direction.<br /><br />In the meantime, the magical and fantastic stuff gets completely glossed over in the beginning, making it hard to understand just what in the hell is going on. I like the idea of this growing from unexplained occurrences to a fully realized magic system, but I really didn't feel it was executed well. <br /><br />The strangest thing is that when I finally got to some action, it was horribly contrived and written with nearly no emotion at all. It was almost as if we were in a hurry to get back to walking around and remarking on the colors of buildings.<br /><br />The world itself is obviously deep and seems interesting enough. Maybe when I have fewer books on my to-read pile, I'll try to slog through this lumbering mess again to see if it gets any better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="99432520391665578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023149205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10341706891814730910">The first in a series about the battle between two opposing forces: chaos and order. Recluce is a city of almost pure order, where people who compromise that order are exiled. The main character, Lerris, is dissatisfied with never getting straight answers and hopelessly bored. I was reminded a bit of Milo from <i>A Phantom Tollbooth</i>. such a person. But, like any good heroic fantasy, this reluctant, unlikely hero does save the day.<br/><br/>The book started very slowly, until Lerris is sent for training, wher</span>
  <span id="freeText10341706891814730910" style="display:none">The first in a series about the battle between two opposing forces: chaos and order. Recluce is a city of almost pure order, where people who compromise that order are exiled. The main character, Lerris, is dissatisfied with never getting straight answers and hopelessly bored. I was reminded a bit of Milo from <i>A Phantom Tollbooth</i>. such a person. But, like any good heroic fantasy, this reluctant, unlikely hero does save the day.<br /><br />The book started very slowly, until Lerris is sent for training, where Modesitt started the world building. His magic system was unorthodox: black wizards are good and white wizards are evil, for example. Once Lerris got settled, the pacing improved. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10341706891814730910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Stefan Bach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach"><img alt="Stefan Bach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603215087p2/24053713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455370894?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Bach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Bach" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach">Stefan Bach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33023712-the-magic-of-recluce">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455370894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16708665235719037378"><i>
  <b>“Be on your way, boy. Just remember, you can always come back, once you discover who you are.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>In a time when readers are demanding for fast-paced, action-packed, non-stop entertaining, easy quick reads - this should have been a safe haven; a resting stop. A <i>recluse.</i><br/><br/>There's nothing worse than unfulfilled potential.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1015123176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015123176" />
    <a title="Shel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2672243-shel"><img alt="Shel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251375325p2/2672243.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1015123176?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shel" href="/user/show/2672243-shel">Shel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6644075-the-magic-of-recluce">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2672243-shel?shelf=beyond-reality-discussions">beyond-reality-discussions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2672243-shel?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2672243-shel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2672243-shel?shelf=kindle-owned">kindle-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015123176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5953176475920798011">Mixed feelings about this one. I enjoyed the worldbuilding and the story, but there were definitely some annoying aspects of the book that kept my rating at three stars. I generally am not a fan of first-person narration, unless it's done really well (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb' title='Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robin Hobb</a> is a master, for example), and Modesitt's writing is passable but nothing special. One of the limitations of first person narratives is, of course, that the reader only can know what the narrator knows; Modesitt got around this by includ</span>
  <span id="freeText5953176475920798011" style="display:none">Mixed feelings about this one. I enjoyed the worldbuilding and the story, but there were definitely some annoying aspects of the book that kept my rating at three stars. I generally am not a fan of first-person narration, unless it's done really well (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a> is a master, for example), and Modesitt's writing is passable but nothing special. One of the limitations of first person narratives is, of course, that the reader only can know what the narrator knows; Modesitt got around this by including several random third-person interludes to explain events happening elsewhere, and they just didn't fit. I think they also were not entirely necessary and the book would have read much more smoothly had the author found a different way to convey the information. <br /><br />The other major irritation were the constant sound effects. At least every few paragraphs started with a <i>Yeee-aaahh....</i> or <i>crreakkkkk...</i> or some other such annoyance. Really, really annoying.<br /><br />All that said, it was an enjoyable story, with an interesting take on the balance between Order and Chaos, and I'm glad I read it. I don't think I'll be picking up the rest of the series, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5953176475920798011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4624141577721692607">Another big long book, and the start of one of those giant epic fantasy sagas.<br/>However, again, I'm not going to go get the sequels.<br/>I like fantasy because it has such potential to expand our concepts of what human society can be, in different and unusual, often dramatic situations.<br/>One can tell, reading this book, that the author is conservative, christian, and non-feminist. This only occasionally intrudes jarringly into the story, but there's absolutely nothing in here that would stretch the comfo</span>
  <span id="freeText4624141577721692607" style="display:none">Another big long book, and the start of one of those giant epic fantasy sagas.<br />However, again, I'm not going to go get the sequels.<br />I like fantasy because it has such potential to expand our concepts of what human society can be, in different and unusual, often dramatic situations.<br />One can tell, reading this book, that the author is conservative, christian, and non-feminist. This only occasionally intrudes jarringly into the story, but there's absolutely nothing in here that would stretch the comfort zone of the most typical inhabitant of stereotypical middle-America.<br />The main character is a bored young man who lives in a utopian society of peace and plenty (where women know their place). But he's bored.<br />His family sends him to a center where the various disaffected (the bored, criminals, feminists) are trained and then sent out of the lovely, ordered kingdom of Recluce to make their way in the dangerous wide world, only possibly to ever return.<br />Our protagonist goes questing and along the way discovers he has the potential to be a super-powerful wizard. MORE TO COME.... in the sequels, of course.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4624141577721692607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10567563243854575932">This book is so good it's not even funny. I read it in China while teaching at a public school and it was nice to come home in the evenings and have this escape.<br/><br/>I thought it started out slow, at an island academy. Things picked up and I liked the skip in time. You really see some good magic system development here with how things decay with the use of magic. This is juxtaposed against a world where people build crafts.<br/><br/>Our hero is in this world and he does a lot of carpentry. I really enjoyed tho</span>
  <span id="freeText10567563243854575932" style="display:none">This book is so good it's not even funny. I read it in China while teaching at a public school and it was nice to come home in the evenings and have this escape.<br /><br />I thought it started out slow, at an island academy. Things picked up and I liked the skip in time. You really see some good magic system development here with how things decay with the use of magic. This is juxtaposed against a world where people build crafts.<br /><br />Our hero is in this world and he does a lot of carpentry. I really enjoyed those small details and can't help but think Modesitt has muddled around in his fair share of workshops.<br /><br />I always recommend this book to members in my fantasy groups. I've read the initial series up to Fall of Angels or Book 6 or whatever and they're all good. This one is the best and I look forward to reading it again soon.</span>

  <span id="freeText5142841039205357312" style="display:none">I don’t DNF books very often, but... Eesh, I have to for the first Recluce book. Read to 8% and couldn’t stand the writing style, main character, or intolerable repetition anymore. <br /><br />I burnt myself out on order/chaos/balance stories a decade ago, and reading the series’ Wikipedia page to see how it ends up killed any possible enthusiasm I had for it. <div id="review_1290441884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290441884" />
    <a title="AndrewP" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3590983-andrewp"><img alt="AndrewP" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285711632p2/3590983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290441884?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AndrewP" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AndrewP" href="/user/show/3590983-andrewp">AndrewP</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25408979-the-magic-of-recluce">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590983-andrewp?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590983-andrewp?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590983-andrewp?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290441884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12602969720929277352">This book is what I would refer to as a traditional, coming of age fantasy story. Misfit teenager destined to become a great hero etc. Personally I don't find anything wrong with this approach when there is sufficient world building and interesting story to back it up.<br/><br/>In this case the author met most of those goals. The world is quite well thought out and the magic system has some interesting ideas that conflict with our preconceived notions of good/evil, black/white, order/chaos. In this sense </span>
  <span id="freeText12602969720929277352" style="display:none">This book is what I would refer to as a traditional, coming of age fantasy story. Misfit teenager destined to become a great hero etc. Personally I don't find anything wrong with this approach when there is sufficient world building and interesting story to back it up.<br /><br />In this case the author met most of those goals. The world is quite well thought out and the magic system has some interesting ideas that conflict with our preconceived notions of good/evil, black/white, order/chaos. In this sense it defiantly kept me entertained. Where the book failed for me was a lack of suspense and emotional connection to the characters. There was also some annoying repetition of the same terms that became tiresome. (Everyone only sweats from their forehead for some reason and the only types of wood worth mentioning are white, red and black oak.)<br /><br />I believe this was the authors first book and there is enough here to make me want to read more of this world. According to what I have read the Recluce books are all set in the same world, but at different points in history, so not really a series in the traditional sense.<br /><br />3.5 stars rounded down to 3 for some repetitive phrasing. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12602969720929277352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bogdan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bogdan" href="/user/show/2537876-bogdan">Bogdan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971589265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15044526868588542143">Wow! This was such a great great book!<br/><br/>I loved the writer style, such an unusual one, with a great deal of attention to the small details, with a conventional evolution of the story, a become of age, but in the same time, an unusual structure to it and not to speak of all the sounds that are described in this book. A delight to read!<br/><br/>And another peculiar thing is the depiction of Good vs Evil not in the usual way, the black is the Order the white is the antagonist way, Disorder.<br/><br/>The main hero fight</span>
  <span id="freeText15044526868588542143" style="display:none">Wow! This was such a great great book!<br /><br />I loved the writer style, such an unusual one, with a great deal of attention to the small details, with a conventional evolution of the story, a become of age, but in the same time, an unusual structure to it and not to speak of all the sounds that are described in this book. A delight to read!<br /><br />And another peculiar thing is the depiction of Good vs Evil not in the usual way, the black is the Order the white is the antagonist way, Disorder.<br /><br />The main hero fights only by protecting itself with a magic rod, there is some fighting not to worry about it, because he represents the Order and tries to find answers to a lot of questions.<br /><br />A lot of time is dedicated to the training of the apprentices, the travel on the roads and the woodcarving and what involves to know this peculiar craft.<br /><br />In short, like I said, this is not your usual fantasy book, but a great version and a still fresh one, after twenty six years passed from it`s first publishing.<br /><br />Amaaaazingg book! I want moree!!</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_144127'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144127.The_Runelords"><img alt="The Runelords (Runelords #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1388196460l/144127._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cc2N+cCl7NaBjxSLfZpiUqsyxU4/YO0o3h1K/kIIKTLd11DZRjS19S9raNqUb7tSI0D31TD1z8yy8fwNgJSnHA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KuBJNaJYK70g99XUO09aeY+srwyAtUm77Xen6cWo/reG+pQVJMlyno4TqYXSuoN5B96dl48ga1+BmxEaBzRwmQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1301649.L_E_Modesitt_Jr_">About L.E. Modesitt Jr.</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1301649.L_E_Modesitt_Jr_"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207333645p3/1301649.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1301649.L_E_Modesitt_Jr_">L.E. Modesitt Jr.
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5632119176487830756">L. E. (Leland Exton) Modesitt, Jr. is an author of science fiction and fantasy novels. He is best known for the fantasy series The Saga of Recluce. He graduated from Williams College in Massachusetts, lived in Washington, D.C. for 20 years, then moved to New Hampshire in 1989 where he met his wife. They relocated to Cedar City, Utah in 1993.<br/><br/>He has worked as a Navy pilot, lifeguard, delivery boy, u</span>
  <span id="freeText5632119176487830756" style="display:none">L. E. (Leland Exton) Modesitt, Jr. is an author of science fiction and fantasy novels. He is best known for the fantasy series The Saga of Recluce. He graduated from Williams College in Massachusetts, lived in Washington, D.C. for 20 years, then moved to New Hampshire in 1989 where he met his wife. They relocated to Cedar City, Utah in 1993.<br /><br />He has worked as a Navy pilot, lifeguard, delivery boy, unpaid radio disc jockey, real estate agent, market research analyst, director of research for a political campaign, legislative assistant for a Congressman, Director of Legislation and Congressional Relations for the United States Environmental Protection Agency, a consultant on environmental, regulatory, and communications issues, and a college lecturer and writer in residence.<br />In addition to his novels, Mr. Modesitt has published technical studies and articles, columns, poetry, and a number of science fiction stories. His first short story, "The Great American Economy", was published in 1973 in Analog Science Fiction and Science Fact.<br /><br />-Wikipedia<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5632119176487830756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Exploring the rich depths of the history of Recluce, Magi\'i of Cyador introduced Lorn, a talented boy born into a family of Magi\'i. A diligent student mage who lacked blind devotion, Lorn was made a lancer officer and shipped off to the frontier--a career that comes with a 50% mortality rate.Having survived his extended stint fighting both barbarian raiders and the giant beasts of the Accursed Forest, Lorn has proven himself to be a fine officer . . . perhaps too fine an officer. As his prowess has grown, so has his number of enemies and rivals. Too much success has made him a marked man. When he returns to his home, both he and his young family become targets while all of Cyad is in upheaval over deadly political infighting. But Lorn is now hardened, a deadly fighter himself, especially when the Empire is at stake.Scion of Cyador is the completion of another grand story in the Recluce saga.Scion of Cyador is the eleventh
